title="Ocean">oceans</a></th></tr><tr><td class="sidebar-content">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">Arctic</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-selflink selflink">Pacific</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Southern_Ocean" title="Southern Ocean">Southern</a></li></ul></td>
</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1063604349">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar a>span,.mw-parser-output .navbar a>abbr{text-decoration:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Five_oceans" title="Template:Five oceans"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Five_oceans" title="Template talk:Five oceans"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Five_oceans&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>Pacific Ocean</b> is the largest and deepest of Earth's five oceanic divisions. It extends from the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">Arctic Ocean</a> in the north to the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Ocean" title="Southern Ocean">Southern Ocean</a> (or, depending on definition, to <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a>) in the south, and is bounded by the continents of <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> in the west and the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a> in the east.
</p><p>At 165,250,000 square kilometers (63,800,000 square miles) in area (as defined with a southern Antarctic border), this largest division of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Ocean" title="World Ocean">World Ocean</a>—and, in turn, the <a href="/wiki/Hydrosphere" title="Hydrosphere">hydrosphere</a>—covers about 46% of Earth's water surface and about 32% of its total surface area, larger than Earth's entire  land area combined 148,000,000 km<sup>2</sup> (57,000,000 sq mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ebc_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-ebc-1">[1]</a></sup> The centers of both the <a href="/wiki/Land_and_water_hemispheres" title="Land and water hemispheres">Water Hemisphere</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">Western Hemisphere</a>, as well as the  <a href="/wiki/Pole_of_inaccessibility#Oceanic_pole_of_inaccessibility" title="Pole of inaccessibility">oceanic pole of inaccessibility</a> are in the Pacific Ocean. Ocean circulation (caused by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coriolis_effect" title="Coriolis effect">Coriolis effect</a>) subdivides it<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> into two largely independent volumes of water, which meet at the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equator</a>: the <b>North</b>(<b>ern</b>) <b>Pacific Ocean</b> and <b>South</b>(<b>ern</b>) <b>Pacific Ocean</b>. The <a href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos_Islands" title="Galápagos Islands">Galápagos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Islands" title="Gilbert Islands">Gilbert Islands</a>, while straddling the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equator</a>, are deemed wholly within the South Pacific.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IHO1953_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-IHO1953-3">[3]</a></sup>
</p><p>Its mean depth is 4,000 meters (13,000 feet).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Challenger_Deep" title="Challenger Deep">Challenger Deep</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Trench" title="Mariana Trench">Mariana Trench</a>, located in the western north Pacific, is the deepest point in the world, reaching a depth of 10,928 meters (35,853 feet).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> The Pacific also contains the deepest point in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Horizon_Deep" title="Horizon Deep">Horizon Deep</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Tonga_Trench" title="Tonga Trench">Tonga Trench</a>, at 10,823 meters (35,509 feet).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> The third deepest point on Earth, the <a href="/wiki/Sirena_Deep" title="Sirena Deep">Sirena Deep</a>, is also located in the Mariana Trench.
</p><p>The western Pacific has many major <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marginal_sea" title="Marginal sea">marginal seas</a>, including but not limited to the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a>, the <a href="/wiki/East_China_Sea" title="East China Sea">East China Sea</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Japan" title="Sea of Japan">Sea of Japan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Okhotsk" title="Sea of Okhotsk">Sea of Okhotsk</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Sea" title="Philippine Sea">Philippine Sea</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Coral_Sea" title="Coral Sea">Coral Sea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Java_Sea" title="Java Sea">Java Sea</a>  and the <a href="/wiki/Tasman_Sea" title="Tasman Sea">Tasman Sea</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the early 16th century, Spanish explorer <a href="/wiki/Vasco_N%C3%BA%C3%B1ez_de_Balboa" title="Vasco Núñez de Balboa">Vasco Núñez de Balboa</a> crossed the <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Panama" title="Isthmus of Panama">Isthmus of Panama</a> in 1513 and sighted the great "Southern Sea" which he named <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Mar del Sur</i></span> (in Spanish). Afterwards, the ocean's current name was coined by Portuguese explorer <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">Ferdinand Magellan</a> during the Spanish <a href="/wiki/Circumnavigation" title="Circumnavigation">circumnavigation</a> of the world in 1521, as he encountered favorable winds on reaching the ocean. He called it <b><span title="Portuguese-language text"><i lang="pt">Mar Pacífico</i></span></b>, which in both Portuguese and Spanish means '<b>peaceful sea'</b>. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_seas_in_the_Pacific_Ocean">Largest seas in the Pacific Ocean</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Largest seas in the Pacific Ocean">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Prehistory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Across the continents of Asia, <a href="/wiki/Australia_(continent)" title="Australia (continent)">Australia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>, more than 25,000 islands, large and small, rise above the surface of the Pacific Ocean. Multiple islands were the shells of erstwhile active <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcanoes</a>, that have lain dormant for thousands of years. Close to the equator through vast areas of blue ocean are a dot of <a href="/wiki/Atoll" title="Atoll">atolls</a> that have over intervals of time been formed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seamounts" title="Seamounts">seamounts</a> as a result of tiny coral islands strung in a ring within surroundings of a central <a href="/wiki/Lagoon" title="Lagoon">lagoon</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_migrations">Early migrations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Early migrations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Peopling_of_Southeast_Asia" title="Peopling of Southeast Asia">Peopling of Southeast Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_peoples" title="Austronesian peoples">Austronesian peoples</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fijian_double_canoe,_model,_Otago_Museum,_2016-01-29.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2901" data-file-width="2798" decoding="async" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Fijian_double_canoe%2C_model%2C_Otago_Museum%2C_2016-01-29.jpg/220px-Fijian_double_canoe%2C_model%2C_Otago_Museum%2C_2016-01-29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Fijian_double_canoe%2C_model%2C_Otago_Museum%2C_2016-01-29.jpg/330px-Fijian_double_canoe%2C_model%2C_Otago_Museum%2C_2016-01-29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Fijian_double_canoe%2C_model%2C_Otago_Museum%2C_2016-01-29.jpg/440px-Fijian_double_canoe%2C_model%2C_Otago_Museum%2C_2016-01-29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fijian_double_canoe,_model,_Otago_Museum,_2016-01-29.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Model of a <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fijian</a> <a href="/wiki/Drua" title="Drua">drua</a>, an example of an <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_peoples" title="Austronesian peoples">Austronesian vessel</a> with a double-canoe (<a href="/wiki/Catamaran" title="Catamaran">catamaran</a>) hull and a <a href="/wiki/Crab_claw_sail" title="Crab claw sail">crab claw sail</a></div></div></div>
<p>Important human migrations occurred in the Pacific in prehistoric times. Modern humans first reached the western Pacific in the <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">Paleolithic</a>, at around 60,000 to 70,000 years ago. Originating from a southern coastal human migration out of Africa, they reached <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mainland_Southeast_Asia" title="Mainland Southeast Asia">Mainland Southeast Asia</a>, the Philippines, <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">New Guinea</a>, and then Australia by making the sea crossing of at least 80 kilometres (50 mi) between <a href="/wiki/Sundaland" title="Sundaland">Sundaland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Australia_(continent)" title="Australia (continent)">Sahul</a>. It is not known with any certainty what level of maritime technology was used by these groups – the presumption is that they used large bamboo rafts which may have been equipped with some sort of sail. The reduction in favourable winds for a crossing to Sahull after 58,000 B.P. fits with the dating of the settlement of Australia, with no later migrations in the prehistoric period. The seafaring abilities of pre-Austronesian residents of Island South-east Asia are confirmed by the settlement of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buka,_Papua_New_Guinea" title="Buka, Papua New Guinea">Buka</a> by 32,000 B.P. and <a href="/wiki/Manus_Island" title="Manus Island">Manus</a> by 25,000 B.P. Journeys of 180 kilometres (110 mi) and 230 kilometres (140 mi) are involved, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>The descendants of these migrations today are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_Asian_peoples" title="East Asian peoples">East Asian peoples</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Negritos" title="Negritos">Negritos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Melanesians" title="Melanesians">Melanesians</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_Australians" title="Indigenous Australians">Indigenous Australians</a>). Their populations in <a href="/wiki/Maritime_Southeast_Asia" title="Maritime Southeast Asia">maritime Southeast Asia</a>, coastal <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">New Guinea</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Island_Melanesia" title="Island Melanesia">Island Melanesia</a> later intermarried with the incoming <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_peoples" title="Austronesian peoples">Austronesian</a> settlers from <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> and the northern <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, but also earlier groups associated with <a href="/wiki/Austroasiatic_languages" title="Austroasiatic languages">Austroasiatic-speakers</a>, resulting in the modern peoples of Island Southeast Asia and Oceania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jett2017_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jett2017-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Waruno2017_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Waruno2017-11">[11]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:442px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chronological_dispersal_of_Austronesian_people_across_the_Pacific.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="425" data-file-width="1053" decoding="async" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Chronological_dispersal_of_Austronesian_people_across_the_Pacific.svg/440px-Chronological_dispersal_of_Austronesian_people_across_the_Pacific.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Chronological_dispersal_of_Austronesian_people_across_the_Pacific.svg/660px-Chronological_dispersal_of_Austronesian_people_across_the_Pacific.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Chronological_dispersal_of_Austronesian_people_across_the_Pacific.svg/880px-Chronological_dispersal_of_Austronesian_people_across_the_Pacific.svg.png 2x" width="440"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chronological_dispersal_of_Austronesian_people_across_the_Pacific.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map showing the migration of the <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_peoples" title="Austronesian peoples">Austronesian peoples</a></div></div></div>
<p>A later seaborne migration is the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austronesian_expansion" title="Austronesian expansion">Austronesian expansion</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_peoples" title="Austronesian peoples">Austronesian peoples</a>. Austronesians originated from the island of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taiwanese_aborigines" title="Taiwanese aborigines">Taiwan</a> c. 3000-1500 BCE. They are associated with distinctive maritime sailing technologies (notably <a href="/wiki/Outrigger_boat" title="Outrigger boat">outrigger boats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catamaran" title="Catamaran">catamarans</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lashed-lug" title="Lashed-lug">lashed-lug</a> boats, and the <a href="/wiki/Crab_claw_sail" title="Crab claw sail">crab claw sail</a>) – it is likely that the progressive development of these technologies were related to the later steps of settlement into Near and Remote Oceania. Starting at around 2200 BCE, Austronesians sailed southwards to settle the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>. From, probably, the <a href="/wiki/Bismarck_Archipelago" title="Bismarck Archipelago">Bismarck Archipelago</a> they crossed the western Pacific to reach the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marianas_Islands" title="Marianas Islands">Marianas Islands</a> by 1500 BCE,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> as well as <a href="/wiki/Palau" title="Palau">Palau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yap" title="Yap">Yap</a> by 1000 BCE. They were the first humans to reach <a href="/wiki/Remote_Oceania" title="Remote Oceania">Remote Oceania</a>, and the first to cross vast distances of open water. They also continued spreading southwards and settling the rest of <a href="/wiki/Maritime_Southeast_Asia" title="Maritime Southeast Asia">Maritime Southeast Asia</a>, reaching <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> by 1500 BCE, and further west to <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Comoros" title="Comoros">Comoros</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a> by around 500 CE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gray-et-al2009_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gray-et-al2009-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pawley2002_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pawley2002-15">[15]</a></sup> More recently, it is suggested that Austronesians expanded already earlier, arriving in the Philippines already in 7000 BCE. Additional earlier migrations into Insular Southeast Asia, associated with Austroasiatic-speakers from Mainland Southeast Asia, are estimated to have taken place already in 15000 BCE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p><p>At around 1300 to 1200 BCE, a branch of the Austronesian migrations known as the <a href="/wiki/Lapita_culture" title="Lapita culture">Lapita culture</a> reached the <a href="/wiki/Bismarck_Archipelago" title="Bismarck Archipelago">Bismarck Archipelago</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a>, and <a href="/wiki/New_Caledonia" title="New Caledonia">New Caledonia</a>. From there, they settled <a href="/wiki/Tonga" title="Tonga">Tonga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Samoa" title="Samoa">Samoa</a> by 900 to 800 BCE. Some also back-migrated northwards in 200 BCE to settle the islands of eastern <a href="/wiki/Micronesia" title="Micronesia">Micronesia</a> (including the <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Islands" title="Caroline Islands">Carolines</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">Marshall Islands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kiribati" title="Kiribati">Kiribati</a>), mixing with earlier Austronesian migrations in the region. This remained the furthest extent of the Austronesian expansion into <a href="/wiki/Polynesia" title="Polynesia">Polynesia</a> until around 700 CE when there was another surge of island exploration. They reached the <a href="/wiki/Cook_Islands" title="Cook Islands">Cook Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tahiti" title="Tahiti">Tahiti</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marquesas" title="Marquesas">Marquesas</a> by 700 CE; <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaiʻi</a> by 900 CE; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapa_Nui" title="Rapa Nui">Rapa Nui</a> by 1000 CE; and finally New Zealand by 1200 CE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gray-et-al2009_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gray-et-al2009-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stanley2004_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stanley2004-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gibbons_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-gibbons-18">[18]</a></sup> Austronesians may have also reached as far as the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>, although evidence for this remains inconclusive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_exploration">European exploration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: European exploration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The first contact of European navigators with the western edge of the Pacific Ocean was made by the Portuguese expeditions of <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_de_Abreu" title="António de Abreu">António de Abreu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Serr%C3%A3o" title="Francisco Serrão">Francisco Serrão</a>, via the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Sunda_Islands" title="Lesser Sunda Islands">Lesser Sunda Islands</a>, to the <a href="/wiki/Maluku_Islands" title="Maluku Islands">Maluku Islands</a>, in 1512,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> and with <a href="/wiki/Jorge_%C3%81lvares" title="Jorge Álvares">Jorge Álvares</a>'s expedition to southern China in 1513,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Porter,_Jonathan_1996_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Porter,_Jonathan_1996-23">[23]</a></sup> both ordered by <a href="/wiki/Afonso_de_Albuquerque" title="Afonso de Albuquerque">Afonso de Albuquerque</a> from <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Malacca" title="Portuguese Malacca">Malacca</a>.
</p><p>The eastern side of the ocean was encountered by Spanish explorer <a href="/wiki/Vasco_N%C3%BA%C3%B1ez_de_Balboa" title="Vasco Núñez de Balboa">Vasco Núñez de Balboa</a> in 1513 after his expedition crossed the <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Panama" title="Isthmus of Panama">Isthmus of Panama</a> and reached a new ocean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ober_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ober-24">[24]</a></sup> He named it <i>Mar del Sur</i> (literally, "Sea of the South" or "South Sea") because the ocean was to the south of the coast of the isthmus where he first observed the Pacific.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:502px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SpanishPacific.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1075" data-file-width="1250" decoding="async" height="430" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/SpanishPacific.svg/500px-SpanishPacific.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/SpanishPacific.svg/750px-SpanishPacific.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/SpanishPacific.svg/1000px-SpanishPacific.svg.png 2x" width="500"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SpanishPacific.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map showing a large number of Spanish expeditions across the Pacific Ocean from the 16th to 18th centuries including the <a href="/wiki/Manila_galleon" title="Manila galleon">Manila galleon</a> route between Acapulco and Manila, the first <a href="/wiki/Transpacific_crossing" title="Transpacific crossing">transpacific</a> trade route in history.</div></div></div>
<p>In 1520, navigator <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">Ferdinand Magellan</a> and his crew were the first to cross the Pacific in recorded history. They were part of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magellan%E2%80%93Elcano_circumnavigation" title="Magellan–Elcano circumnavigation">Spanish expedition</a> to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spice_Islands" title="Spice Islands">Spice Islands</a> that would eventually result in the first world <a href="/wiki/Circumnavigation" title="Circumnavigation">circumnavigation</a>. Magellan called the ocean <i>Pacífico</i> (or "Pacific" meaning, "peaceful") because, after sailing through the stormy seas off <a href="/wiki/Cape_Horn" title="Cape Horn">Cape Horn</a>, the expedition found calm waters. The ocean was often called the <i>Sea of Magellan</i> in his honor until the eighteenth century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Magellan stopped at one uninhabited Pacific island before stopping at <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a> in March 1521.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Although Magellan himself died in the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> in 1521, Spanish navigator <a href="/wiki/Juan_Sebasti%C3%A1n_Elcano" title="Juan Sebastián Elcano">Juan Sebastián Elcano</a> led the remains of the expedition back to Spain across the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a> and round the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape of Good Hope</a>, completing the first world circumnavigation in 1522.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oceanario_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-oceanario-27">[27]</a></sup> Sailing around and east of the Moluccas, between 1525 and 1527, Portuguese expeditions encountered the <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Islands" title="Caroline Islands">Caroline Islands</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Aru_Islands_Regency" title="Aru Islands Regency">Aru Islands</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Whiteway_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Whiteway-30">[30]</a></sup> In 1542–43 the Portuguese also reached Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1564, five Spanish ships carrying 379 soldiers crossed the ocean from Mexico led by <a href="/wiki/Miguel_L%C3%B3pez_de_Legazpi" title="Miguel López de Legazpi">Miguel López de Legazpi</a>, and colonized the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Islands" title="Mariana Islands">Mariana Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HendersonDelpar2000_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-HendersonDelpar2000-32">[32]</a></sup> For the remainder of the 16th century, Spain maintained military and mercantile control, with ships sailing from Mexico and <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> across the Pacific Ocean to the Philippines via <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a>, and establishing the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">Spanish East Indies</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Manila_galleon" title="Manila galleon">Manila galleons</a> operated for two and a half centuries, linking <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">Manila</a> and <a href="/wiki/Acapulco" title="Acapulco">Acapulco</a>, in one of the longest trade routes in history. Spanish expeditions also arrived at <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Marquesas_Islands" title="Marquesas Islands">Marquesas</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cook_Islands" title="Cook Islands">Cook Islands</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Admiralty_Islands" title="Admiralty Islands">Admiralty Islands</a> in the South Pacific.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fernandez-Armesto_2006_305–307_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fernandez-Armesto_2006_305–307-33">[33]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Waldseemuller_map_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="7590" data-file-width="13708" decoding="async" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Waldseemuller_map_2.jpg/220px-Waldseemuller_map_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Waldseemuller_map_2.jpg/330px-Waldseemuller_map_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Waldseemuller_map_2.jpg/440px-Waldseemuller_map_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Waldseemuller_map_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Universalis Cosmographia</i>, the <a href="/wiki/Waldseem%C3%BCller_map" title="Waldseemüller map">Waldseemüller map</a> dated 1507, from a time when the nature of the Americas was ambiguous, particularly North America, as a possible part of Asia, was the first map to show the Americas separating two distinct oceans. South America was generally considered a "new world" and shows the name "America" for the first time, after <a href="/wiki/Amerigo_Vespucci" title="Amerigo Vespucci">Amerigo Vespucci</a></div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Exploration_of_the_Pacific" title="Exploration of the Pacific">Exploration of the Pacific</a></div>
<p>Later, in the quest for <a href="/wiki/Terra_Australis" title="Terra Australis">Terra Australis</a> ("the [great] Southern Land"), Spanish explorations in the 17th century, such as the expedition led by the Portuguese navigator <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Fernandes_de_Queir%C3%B3s" title="Pedro Fernandes de Queirós">Pedro Fernandes de Queirós</a>, arrived at the <a href="/wiki/Pitcairn_Islands" title="Pitcairn Islands">Pitcairn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</a> archipelagos, and sailed the <a href="/wiki/Torres_Strait" title="Torres Strait">Torres Strait</a> between Australia and New Guinea, named after navigator <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_Vaz_de_Torres" title="Luís Vaz de Torres">Luís Vaz de Torres</a>. Dutch explorers, sailing around southern Africa, also engaged in exploration and trade; <a href="/wiki/Willem_Janszoon" title="Willem Janszoon">Willem Janszoon</a>, made the first completely documented European landing in Australia (1606), in <a href="/wiki/Cape_York_Peninsula" title="Cape York Peninsula">Cape York Peninsula</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Abel_Tasman" title="Abel Tasman">Abel Janszoon Tasman</a> circumnavigated and landed on parts of the Australian continental coast and arrived at <a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">Tasmania</a> and New Zealand in 1642.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 16th and 17th centuries, Spain considered the Pacific Ocean a <i><a href="/wiki/Mare_clausum" title="Mare clausum">mare clausum</a></i>—a sea closed to other naval powers. As the only known entrance from the Atlantic, the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Magellan" title="Strait of Magellan">Strait of Magellan</a> was at times patrolled by fleets sent to prevent the entrance of non-Spanish ships. On the western side of the Pacific Ocean the Dutch threatened the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Spanish Philippines</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lytle_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-lytle-36">[36]</a></sup>
</p><p>The 18th century marked the beginning of major exploration by the Russians in <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Aleutian_Islands" title="Aleutian Islands">Aleutian Islands</a>, such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_Kamchatka_expedition" title="First Kamchatka expedition">First Kamchatka expedition</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_Expedition" title="Great Northern Expedition">Great Northern Expedition</a>, led by the Danish Russian navy officer <a href="/wiki/Vitus_Bering" title="Vitus Bering">Vitus Bering</a>. Spain also sent <a href="/wiki/Spanish_expeditions_to_the_Pacific_Northwest" title="Spanish expeditions to the Pacific Northwest">expeditions to the Pacific Northwest</a>, reaching <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Island" title="Vancouver Island">Vancouver Island</a> in southern Canada, and Alaska. The French explored and colonized <a href="/wiki/Polynesia" title="Polynesia">Polynesia</a>, and the British made three voyages with <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a> to the South Pacific and Australia, <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>, and the North American <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Northwest" title="Pacific Northwest">Pacific Northwest</a>. In 1768, <a href="/wiki/Pierre-Antoine_V%C3%A9ron" title="Pierre-Antoine Véron">Pierre-Antoine Véron</a>, a young <a href="/wiki/Astronomer" title="Astronomer">astronomer</a> accompanying <a href="/wiki/Louis_Antoine_de_Bougainville" title="Louis Antoine de Bougainville">Louis Antoine de Bougainville</a> on his voyage of exploration, established the width of the Pacific with precision for the first time in history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams2004_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Williams2004-37">[37]</a></sup> One of the earliest voyages of scientific exploration was organized by Spain in the <a href="/wiki/Malaspina_Expedition" title="Malaspina Expedition">Malaspina Expedition</a> of 1789–1794. It sailed vast areas of the Pacific, from Cape Horn to Alaska, Guam and the Philippines, New Zealand, Australia, and the South Pacific.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fernandez-Armesto_2006_305–307_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fernandez-Armesto_2006_305–307-33">[33]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 284.66666666667px"><div style="width: 284.66666666667px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 282.66666666667px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carta_universal_en_que_se_contiene_todo_lo_que_del_mundo_se_ha_descubierto_fasta_agora_hizola_Diego_Ribero_cosmographo_de_su_magestad,_ano_de_1529,_en_Sevilla.jpg" title="Made in 1529, the Diogo Ribeiro map was the first to show the Pacific at about its proper size"><img alt="Made in 1529, the Diogo Ribeiro map was the first to show the Pacific at about its proper size" data-file-height="2324" data-file-width="5471" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Carta_universal_en_que_se_contiene_todo_lo_que_del_mundo_se_ha_descubierto_fasta_agora_hizola_Diego_Ribero_cosmographo_de_su_magestad%2C_ano_de_1529%2C_en_Sevilla.jpg/424px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Carta_universal_en_que_se_contiene_todo_lo_que_del_mundo_se_ha_descubierto_fasta_agora_hizola_Diego_Ribero_cosmographo_de_su_magestad%2C_ano_de_1529%2C_en_Sevilla.jpg/636px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Carta_universal_en_que_se_contiene_todo_lo_que_del_mundo_se_ha_descubierto_fasta_agora_hizola_Diego_Ribero_cosmographo_de_su_magestad%2C_ano_de_1529%2C_en_Sevilla.jpg/848px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="283"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>Made in 1529, the <a href="/wiki/Diogo_Ribeiro" title="Diogo Ribeiro">Diogo Ribeiro</a> map was the first to show the Pacific at about its proper size
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 188.66666666667px"><div style="width: 188.66666666667px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 186.66666666667px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_compleat_chart_of_the_coast_of_Asia_and_America_with_the_great_South_Sea_-_R.W._Seale_del._et_sculp._NYPL465242.tiff" title="Map of the Pacific Ocean during European Exploration, circa 1754."><img alt="Map of the Pacific Ocean during European Exploration, circa 1754." data-file-height="3315" data-file-width="5158" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/A_compleat_chart_of_the_coast_of_Asia_and_America_with_the_great_South_Sea_-_R.W._Seale_del._et_sculp._NYPL465242.tiff/lossless-page1-280px-A_compleat_chart_of_the_coast_of_Asia_and_America_with_the_great_South_Sea_-_R.W._Seale_del._et_sculp._NYPL465242.tiff.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/A_compleat_chart_of_the_coast_of_Asia_and_America_with_the_great_South_Sea_-_R.W._Seale_del._et_sculp._NYPL465242.tiff/lossless-page1-420px-A_compleat_chart_of_the_coast_of_Asia_and_America_with_the_great_South_Sea_-_R.W._Seale_del._et_sculp._NYPL465242.tiff.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/A_compleat_chart_of_the_coast_of_Asia_and_America_with_the_great_South_Sea_-_R.W._Seale_del._et_sculp._NYPL465242.tiff/lossless-page1-560px-A_compleat_chart_of_the_coast_of_Asia_and_America_with_the_great_South_Sea_-_R.W._Seale_del._et_sculp._NYPL465242.tiff.png 2x" width="187"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>Map of the Pacific Ocean during European Exploration, circa 1754.
</p>
</div>
</div></li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 175.33333333333px"><div style="width: 175.33333333333px">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Imperialism">New Imperialism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: New Imperialism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/New_Imperialism" title="New Imperialism">New Imperialism</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bathyscaphe_Trieste_with_USS_Lewis_(DE-535)_over_the_Marianas_Trench,_23_January_1960_(NH_96797).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3058" data-file-width="4112" decoding="async" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Bathyscaphe_Trieste_with_USS_Lewis_%28DE-535%29_over_the_Marianas_Trench%2C_23_January_1960_%28NH_96797%29.jpg/220px-Bathyscaphe_Trieste_with_USS_Lewis_%28DE-535%29_over_the_Marianas_Trench%2C_23_January_1960_%28NH_96797%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Bathyscaphe_Trieste_with_USS_Lewis_%28DE-535%29_over_the_Marianas_Trench%2C_23_January_1960_%28NH_96797%29.jpg/330px-Bathyscaphe_Trieste_with_USS_Lewis_%28DE-535%29_over_the_Marianas_Trench%2C_23_January_1960_%28NH_96797%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Bathyscaphe_Trieste_with_USS_Lewis_%28DE-535%29_over_the_Marianas_Trench%2C_23_January_1960_%28NH_96797%29.jpg/440px-Bathyscaphe_Trieste_with_USS_Lewis_%28DE-535%29_over_the_Marianas_Trench%2C_23_January_1960_%28NH_96797%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bathyscaphe_Trieste_with_USS_Lewis_(DE-535)_over_the_Marianas_Trench,_23_January_1960_(NH_96797).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The bathyscaphe <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bathyscaphe_Trieste" title="Bathyscaphe Trieste">Trieste</a></i>, before her record dive to the bottom of the <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Trench" title="Mariana Trench">Mariana Trench</a>, 23 January 1960</div></div></div>
<p>Growing <a href="/wiki/Imperialism" title="Imperialism">imperialism</a> during the 19th century resulted in the occupation of much of Oceania by European powers, and later Japan and the United States. Significant contributions to oceanographic knowledge were made by the voyages of <a href="/wiki/HMS_Beagle" title="HMS Beagle">HMS <i>Beagle</i></a> in the 1830s, with <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">Charles Darwin</a> aboard;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/HMS_Challenger_(1858)" title="HMS Challenger (1858)">HMS <i>Challenger</i></a> during the 1870s;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/USS_Tuscarora_(1861)" title="USS Tuscarora (1861)">USS <i>Tuscarora</i></a> (1873–76);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> and the German <i>Gazelle</i> (1874–76).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TahitiDupetitThouars.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1162" data-file-width="2247" decoding="async" height="114" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/TahitiDupetitThouars.jpg/220px-TahitiDupetitThouars.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/TahitiDupetitThouars.jpg/330px-TahitiDupetitThouars.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/TahitiDupetitThouars.jpg/440px-TahitiDupetitThouars.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TahitiDupetitThouars.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Abel_Aubert_du_Petit-Thouars" title="Abel Aubert du Petit-Thouars">Abel Aubert du Petit-Thouars</a> taking over <a href="/wiki/Tahiti" title="Tahiti">Tahiti</a> on 9 September 1842</div></div></div>
<p>In Oceania, France obtained a leading position as imperial power after making <a href="/wiki/Tahiti" title="Tahiti">Tahiti</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Caledonia" title="New Caledonia">New Caledonia</a> protectorates in 1842 and 1853, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Asiapacific_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Asiapacific-43">[43]</a></sup> After navy visits to <a href="/wiki/Easter_Island" title="Easter Island">Easter Island</a> in 1875 and 1887, Chilean navy officer <a href="/wiki/Policarpo_Toro" title="Policarpo Toro">Policarpo Toro</a> negotiated the incorporation of the island into Chile with native <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapanui" title="Rapanui">Rapanui</a> in 1888. By occupying Easter Island, Chile joined the imperial nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sater_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-sater-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 53">: 53 </span></sup> By 1900 nearly all Pacific islands were in control of Britain, France, United States, Germany, Japan, and Chile.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Asiapacific_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-Asiapacific-43">[43]</a></sup>
</p><p>Although the United States gained control of <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a> and the Philippines from Spain in 1898,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TewariAlvarez2008_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-TewariAlvarez2008-45">[45]</a></sup> Japan controlled most of the western Pacific by 1914 and occupied many other islands during the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_War" title="Pacific War">Pacific War</a>; however, by the end of that war, Japan was defeated and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">U.S. Pacific Fleet</a> was the virtual master of the ocean. The Japanese-ruled <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="Northern Mariana Islands">Northern Mariana Islands</a> came under the control of the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Since the end of World War II, many former colonies in the Pacific have become independent <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">states</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iss007e10807.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1853" data-file-width="3032" decoding="async" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Iss007e10807.jpg/220px-Iss007e10807.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Iss007e10807.jpg/330px-Iss007e10807.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Iss007e10807.jpg/440px-Iss007e10807.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iss007e10807.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sunset over the Pacific Ocean as seen from the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a>. tops of <a href="/wiki/Cumulonimbus_cloud" title="Cumulonimbus cloud">thunderclouds</a> are also visible.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pacific_Basin_Island_Geography.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Pacific_Basin_Island_Geography.jpg/280px-Pacific_Basin_Island_Geography.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Pacific_Basin_Island_Geography.jpg/420px-Pacific_Basin_Island_Geography.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Pacific_Basin_Island_Geography.jpg/560px-Pacific_Basin_Island_Geography.jpg 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pacific_Basin_Island_Geography.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The island geography of the Pacific Ocean Basin</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pacific_Culture_Areas.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="908" data-file-width="1396" decoding="async" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Pacific_Culture_Areas.png/280px-Pacific_Culture_Areas.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Pacific_Culture_Areas.png/420px-Pacific_Culture_Areas.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Pacific_Culture_Areas.png/560px-Pacific_Culture_Areas.png 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pacific_Culture_Areas.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Regions, island nations and territories of <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Pacific separates Asia and Australia from the Americas. It may be further subdivided by the equator into northern (North Pacific) and southern (South Pacific) portions. It extends from the <a href="/wiki/Antarctic" title="Antarctic">Antarctic</a> region in the South to the <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a> in the north.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ebc_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-ebc-1">[1]</a></sup> The Pacific Ocean encompasses approximately one-third of the Earth's surface, having an area of 165,200,000 km<sup>2</sup> (63,800,000 sq mi)— larger than Earth's entire landmass combined, 150,000,000 km<sup>2</sup> (58,000,000 sq mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup>
</p><p>Extending approximately 15,500 km (9,600 mi) from the <a href="/wiki/Bering_Sea" title="Bering Sea">Bering Sea</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a> to the northern extent of the circumpolar <a href="/wiki/Southern_Ocean" title="Southern Ocean">Southern Ocean</a> at <a href="/wiki/60th_parallel_south" title="60th parallel south">60°S</a> (older definitions extend it to <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Ross_Sea" title="Ross Sea">Ross Sea</a>), the Pacific reaches its greatest east–west width at about <a href="/wiki/5th_parallel_north" title="5th parallel north">5°N latitude</a>, where it stretches approximately 19,800 km (12,300 mi) from Indonesia to the coast of <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>—halfway around the world, and more than five times the diameter of the Moon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nuttall2005_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nuttall2005-48">[48]</a></sup> Its geographic center is in eastern <a href="/wiki/Kiribati" title="Kiribati">Kiribati</a> south of <a href="/wiki/Kiritimati" title="Kiritimati">Kiritimati</a>, just west from <a href="/wiki/Starbuck_Island" title="Starbuck Island">Starbuck Island</a> at <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1073938472" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Pacific_Ocean&amp;params=4.97_S_158.75_W_type:landmark_region:FR_scale:10000"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">4°58′S</span> <span class="longitude">158°45′W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">4.97°S 158.75°W</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">-4.97; -158.75</span></span></span></a></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-"><a href="#cite_note-">[49]</a></sup> The lowest known point on Earth—the <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Trench" title="Mariana Trench">Mariana Trench</a>—lies 10,911 m (35,797 <a href="/wiki/Foot_(unit)" title="Foot (unit)">ft</a>; 5,966 <a href="/wiki/Fathom" title="Fathom">fathoms</a>) below sea level. Its average depth is 4,280 m (14,040 ft; 2,340 fathoms), putting the total water volume at roughly 710,000,000 km<sup>3</sup> (170,000,000 cu mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ebc_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-ebc-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p><p>Due to the effects of <a href="/wiki/Plate_tectonics" title="Plate tectonics">plate tectonics</a>, the Pacific Ocean is currently shrinking by roughly 2.5 cm (1 in) per year on three sides, roughly averaging 0.52 km<sup>2</sup> (0.20 sq mi) a year. By contrast, the Atlantic Ocean is increasing in size.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Young2009_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Young2009-51">[51]</a></sup>
</p><p>Along the Pacific Ocean's irregular western margins lie many seas, the largest of which are the <a href="/wiki/Celebes_Sea" title="Celebes Sea">Celebes Sea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coral_Sea" title="Coral Sea">Coral Sea</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_China_Sea" title="East China Sea">East China Sea</a> (East Sea), <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Sea" title="Philippine Sea">Philippine Sea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Japan" title="Sea of Japan">Sea of Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a> (South Sea), <a href="/wiki/Sulu_Sea" title="Sulu Sea">Sulu Sea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tasman_Sea" title="Tasman Sea">Tasman Sea</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yellow_Sea" title="Yellow Sea">Yellow Sea</a> (West Sea of Korea). The <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Indonesia#Indonesian_Seaway" title="Geology of Indonesia">Indonesian Seaway</a> (including the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Malacca" title="Strait of Malacca">Strait of Malacca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Torres_Strait" title="Torres Strait">Torres Strait</a>) joins the Pacific and the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a> to the west, and <a href="/wiki/Drake_Passage" title="Drake Passage">Drake Passage</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Magellan" title="Strait of Magellan">Strait of Magellan</a> link the Pacific with the Atlantic Ocean on the east. To the north, the <a href="/wiki/Bering_Strait" title="Bering Strait">Bering Strait</a> connects the Pacific with the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">Arctic Ocean</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Organization1953_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Organization1953-52">[52]</a></sup>
</p><p>As the Pacific straddles the <a href="/wiki/180th_meridian" title="180th meridian">180th meridian</a>, the <i>West Pacific</i> (or <i>western Pacific</i>, near Asia) is in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Hemisphere" title="Eastern Hemisphere">Eastern Hemisphere</a>, while the <i>East Pacific</i> (or <i>eastern Pacific</i>, near the Americas) is in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">Western Hemisphere</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lydia_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lydia-53">[53]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Southern Pacific Ocean harbors the <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Indian_Ridge" title="Southeast Indian Ridge">Southeast Indian Ridge</a> crossing from south of Australia turning into the <a href="/wiki/Pacific-Antarctic_Ridge" title="Pacific-Antarctic Ridge">Pacific-Antarctic Ridge</a> (north of the <a href="/wiki/South_Pole" title="South Pole">South Pole</a>) and merges with another ridge (south of South America) to form the <a href="/wiki/East_Pacific_Rise" title="East Pacific Rise">East Pacific Rise</a> which also connects with another ridge (south of North America) which overlooks the <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Fuca_Ridge" title="Juan de Fuca Ridge">Juan de Fuca Ridge</a>.
</p><p>For most of Magellan's voyage from the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Magellan" title="Strait of Magellan">Strait of Magellan</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, the explorer indeed found the ocean peaceful; however, the Pacific is not always peaceful. Many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_storm" title="Tropical storm">tropical storms</a> batter the islands of the Pacific.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> The lands around the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Rim" title="Pacific Rim">Pacific Rim</a> are full of <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcanoes</a> and often affected by <a href="/wiki/Earthquake" title="Earthquake">earthquakes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Murphy1979_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Murphy1979-55">[55]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tsunami" title="Tsunami">Tsunamis</a>, caused by underwater earthquakes, have devastated many islands and in some cases destroyed entire towns.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bryant2008_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bryant2008-56">[56]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Martin_Waldseem%C3%BCller" title="Martin Waldseemüller">Martin Waldseemüller</a> map of 1507 was the first to show the Americas separating two distinct oceans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Later, the <a href="/wiki/Diogo_Ribeiro" title="Diogo Ribeiro">Diogo Ribeiro</a> map of 1529 was the first to show the Pacific at about its proper size.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bordering_countries_and_territories">Bordering countries and territories</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Bordering countries and territories">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sovereign_nations">Sovereign nations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Sovereign nations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r998391716" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="div-col" style="column-width: 20em;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a></li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Landmasses_and_islands">Landmasses and islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pacific_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Landmasses and islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands" title="Pacific Islands">Pacific Islands</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:South_Tarawa_from_the_air.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1569" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="115" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/South_Tarawa_from_the_air.jpg/220px-South_Tarawa_from_the_air.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/South_Tarawa_from_the_air.jpg/330px-South_Tarawa_from_the_air.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/South_Tarawa_from_the_air.jpg/440px-South_Tarawa_from_the_air.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:South_Tarawa_from_the_air.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tarawa_Atoll" title="Tarawa Atoll">Tarawa Atoll</a> in the Republic of <a href="/wiki/Kiribati" title="Kiribati">Kiribati</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Pacific Ocean has most of the islands in the world. There are about 25,000 islands in the Pacific Ocean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> The islands entirely within the Pacific Ocean can be divided into three main groups known as <a href="/wiki/Micronesia" title="Micronesia">Micronesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Melanesia" title="Melanesia">Melanesia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Polynesia" title="Polynesia">Polynesia</a>. Micronesia, which lies north of the equator and west of the <a href="/wiki/International_Date_Line" title="International Date Line">International Date Line</a>, includes the <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Islands" title="Mariana Islands">Mariana Islands</a> in the northwest, the <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Islands" title="Caroline Islands">Caroline Islands</a> in the center, the <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">Marshall Islands</a> to the east and the islands of <a href="/wiki/Kiribati" title="Kiribati">Kiribati</a> in the southeast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AAE_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-AAE-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LalFortune2000p63_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-LalFortune2000p63-63">[63]</a></sup>
</p><p>Melanesia, to the southwest, includes <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">New Guinea</a>, the world's second largest island after <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> and by far the largest of the Pacific islands. The other main Melanesian groups from north to south are the <a href="/wiki/Bismarck_Archipelago" title="Bismarck Archipelago">Bismarck Archipelago</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_Islands" title="Santa Cruz Islands">Santa Cruz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Caledonia" title="New Caledonia">New Caledonia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-West2009_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-West2009-64">[64]</a></sup>
</p><p>The largest area, <a href="/wiki/Polynesia" title="Polynesia">Polynesia</a>, stretching from <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a> in the north to New Zealand in the south, also encompasses <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tokelau" title="Tokelau">Tokelau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samoa" title="Samoa">Samoa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tonga" title="Tonga">Tonga</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kermadec_Islands" title="Kermadec Islands">Kermadec Islands</a> to the west, the <a href="/wiki/Cook_Islands" title="Cook Islands">Cook Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Society_Islands" title="Society Islands">Society Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Austral_Islands" title="Austral Islands">Austral Islands</a> in the center, and the <a href="/wiki/Marquesas_Islands" title="Marquesas Islands">Marquesas Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tuamotus" title="Tuamotus">Tuamotu</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mangareva_Islands" title="Mangareva Islands">Mangareva Islands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Easter_Island" title="Easter Island">Easter Island</a> to the east.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DunfordRidgell1996_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-DunfordRidgell1996-65">[65]</a></sup>
</p><p>Islands in the Pacific Ocean are of four basic types: continental islands, high islands, coral reefs and uplifted coral platforms. Continental islands lie outside the andesite line and include New Guinea, the islands of New Zealand, and the Philippines. Some of these islands are structurally associated with nearby continents. High islands are of volcanic origin, and many contain active volcanoes. Among these are <a href="/wiki/Bougainville_Island" title="Bougainville Island">Bougainville</a>, Hawaii, and the Solomon Islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GillespieClague2009_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-GillespieClague2009-66">[66]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">coral reefs</a> of the South Pacific are low-lying structures that have built up on basaltic lava flows under the ocean's surface. One of the most dramatic is the <a href="/wiki/Great_Barrier_Reef" title="Great Barrier Reef">Great Barrier Reef</a> off northeastern Australia with chains of reef patches. A second island type formed of coral is the uplifted coral platform, which is usually slightly larger than the low coral islands. Examples include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Banaba_Island" title="Banaba Island">Banaba</a> (formerly Ocean Island) and <a href="/wiki/Makatea" title="Makatea">Makatea</a> in the Tuamotu group of <a href="/wiki/French_Polynesia" title="French Polynesia">French Polynesia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 215px"><div style="width: 215px">
